  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/27877579-olaf-verboon">Olaf Verboon</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    It was stated that he was found by the Skandian and taken back to his city, after unsuccesfully returning to the beach to find the Kokiri. He is menti<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    It was stated that he was found by the Skandian and taken back to his city, after unsuccesfully returning to the beach to find the Kokiri. He is mentioned near the end of the book as providing the intel that the back-up for Arisaka is on its way and that the battle needs to be now. How this intel is brought to the reclusive fort is a bit of a plot hole in my opinion.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15462727929028211496">The Emperor of Nihon-Ja (Ranger's Apprentice, #10), John Flanagan<br/><br/>The name Nihon-Ja is based on the name of Japan, Nihon-Koku. The Emperor of Nihon-Ja is the tenth installment of the Ranger's Apprentice book series by Australian author John Flanagan. The book was released in Australia on 1 November 2010.<br/><br/>Horace (the knight) is missing. Months have passed since he was sent on a military mission to the court of the Emperor of Nihon-Ja with his friend, former wardmate, and Scribeschool apprentice Geo</span>
  <span id="freeText15462727929028211496" style="display:none">The Emperor of Nihon-Ja (Ranger's Apprentice, #10), John Flanagan<br /><br />The name Nihon-Ja is based on the name of Japan, Nihon-Koku. The Emperor of Nihon-Ja is the tenth installment of the Ranger's Apprentice book series by Australian author John Flanagan. The book was released in Australia on 1 November 2010.<br /><br />Horace (the knight) is missing. Months have passed since he was sent on a military mission to the court of the Emperor of Nihon-Ja with his friend, former wardmate, and Scribeschool apprentice George, but he has failed to return. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Halt (a legendary Ranger), Will (another legendary Ranger), Selethen (the leader of the Arridi, a nomadic desert tribe) and Alyss (a Diplomatic Service Courier) are in Toscana overseeing a demonstration using tight formations to overcome more skilled opponents. When Evanlyn (also known as the Crown Princess Cassandra) arrives telling of Horace's absence, The Araluens and Selethen embark on a Skandian duty ship to find Horace.<br /><br />They find that Horace has become embroiled in Nihon-Ja politics. The arrogant Senshi sect, the Nihon-Ja warrior class, has rebelled against the rightful Emperor Shigeru out of fear he will usurp their influence in the country. Shigeru, though a Senshi himself, is also a man of the people and has been trying to reform his nation's strict social system. Horace has chosen to stay and lend support to the deposed ruler. Pursued by the rebel leader and master swordsman Arisaka, Horace and Shigeru flee along with Shigeru's cousin and guard Shukin. <br /><br />Their only hope is to find to the fabled fortress of Ran-Koshi, which is mentioned in a legend and said to have impossibly high walls. The three lead their small entourage of 50 Senshi around the native villages recruiting Kikori, lumberjacks native to the area.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و چهارم ماه سپتامبر سال 2018 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: امپراتور نیهون-جا: کتاب دهم از سری جنگاور جوان (کارآموز رنجر)؛ نویسنده: جان فلنگن؛<br /><br />هنگامی‌ که «هوراس» به سرزمین عجیب‌ و غریب «نيهون جا» سفر می‌کند، طولی نمیکشد که خود را درنبردی می‌بیند كه به او مربوط نيست؛ زمانی که امپراتور «نيهون جا» سرنگون‌شده است، پادشاهی در لبه هرج‌ و مرج است؛ تنها هوراس، ویل و همراهانش از آرالئون، می‌توانند امپراتور را به تخت بازگردانند. ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_351964708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351964708" />
    <a title="Chesra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10168952-chesra"><img alt="Chesra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340067460p2/10168952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351964708?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chesra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chesra" href="/user/show/10168952-chesra">Chesra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10168952-chesra?shelf=borrowed-books">borrowed-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351964708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3599724030459608559">(I just feel the need to explain the 2-stars rating here.)<br/><br/>I’ve been reading the Ranger’s Apprentice series, written by John Flanagan, for the past two years thanks to my good friend Kara. This is the final book, The Emperor of Nihon-Ja and I spent the entire night reading it, instead of going to bed. Haha.<br/><br/>I don’t think I’ve ever done a book review for this series because I’ve always been relatively impartial about it; it’s an okay book for me. Not something I would buy myself each time it comes </span>
  <span id="freeText3599724030459608559" style="display:none">(I just feel the need to explain the 2-stars rating here.)<br /><br />I’ve been reading the Ranger’s Apprentice series, written by John Flanagan, for the past two years thanks to my good friend Kara. This is the final book, The Emperor of Nihon-Ja and I spent the entire night reading it, instead of going to bed. Haha.<br /><br />I don’t think I’ve ever done a book review for this series because I’ve always been relatively impartial about it; it’s an okay book for me. Not something I would buy myself each time it comes out, but it’s an intriguing read with characters that develop throughout the series and interesting, if sometimes cliched, plotlines.<br /><br />But something in the last book of the series irritated me so damn much I actually had to sit down and write it.<br /><br />So the basic premise for the 10th book is this; the Emperor of Nihon-Ja is usurped from his throne, so our heroes go and save him. You know how that ends. Anyway, along for the ride this time is Evanlyn, a girl we’ve met in the previous books, and Alyss, Will’s childhood friend-turned-sweetheart. Will is our main character, the titular Ranger’s Apprentice. But this isn’t about him.<br /><br />The books have established in the past 3-4 books that Alyss and Will are together, probably for a few years or more. Now when Evanlyn and Will were featured in the same book together, way back in book 3, it was shown that Evanlyn was interested but Will only saw her as a friend (and some spoiler reasons, which I shan’t go into), and that romantic thread was cut off.<br /><br />Cut to book 10, where Alyss is still constantly jealous over Evanlyn. I’m serious. Alyss is a tall, beautiful, self-aware woman who speaks multiple languages and can kayak, and she spends most of the book being mean and petty to the ONLY OTHER FEMALE CHARACTER IN THE BOOK THANKS TO A LONG-AGO CRUSH WHOSE ROMANCE NEVER EVEN HAPPENED.<br /><br />I mean, hello? I was seriously so annoyed. Every time I flipped over to the parts of the book which had their POV, it was always like that. And even Evanlyn, who could have just cleared it up that she wasn’t interested in Will far earlier in the book, just responds to this in the same manner. They are both so hostile to each other, which I just cannot understand. Every time it switches to their POV, there is always a mention of how much they cannot stand the other girl. <br /><br />I would have understood if the characters were teenagers. But these two women are around their early twenties; I cannot imagine them fighting over a guy like that. Especially since it’s established that Alyss is a level-headed character and Evanlyn, while impulsive, has very good instincts. All throughout the book I was like, “What the fuck, author. WHAT THE FUCK.”<br /><br />I mean of course in the end everything resolves itself, but wow, so they had to fight a gigantic monster together in a life-or-death struggle before they can actually see eye-to-eye? They spend months preparing for a war in a fortress as roommates, you’re telling me things couldn’t have somehow resolved themselves within that timeframe? SERIOUSLY? I have to be about 50 pages before the book’s resolution before the two of them become friends?!<br /><br />I’m just really disappointed with how John Flanagan treated these two amazing women in his book. He’s featured them both as holding out on their own in their own adventures, and even in this book they do that, but they can’t get along with their fellow women? I mean, this jealousy and hostility is completely against their character. I can’t believe he even let it be the defining point of these two women in the book.<br /><br />This sort of portrayal gives me a headache. Please. Women do not fight over men as much as movies and books like to think. There is plenty of common ground. Just because women are as stereotyped this way, doesn’t mean you have to keep encouraging it.<br /><br />Plus it even makes canon make no sense. Will and Alyss have been together for a while, and she’s still jealous over this childhood crush that happened probably five or so years ago? I just find it so unrealistic. So Alyss happens to be a perfectly capable diplomat, who can stay calm in dangerous meetings, but she’s irrational when it comes to Will?<br /><br />Just. AAAARRRGGGHHH. This book left a bad taste in my mouth, which I wish it hadn’t. It’s the last book in the series, and I wanted to enjoy it. Instead I got this. I liked Alyss and Evanlyn so much when they both got their time in previous books and I was so excited to see them in this book, and I got this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3599724030459608559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_121796224" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121796224" />
    <a title="Stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1868161-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544150649p2/1868161.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121796224?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie" href="/user/show/1868161-stephanie">Stephanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399255007" href="/book/show/8404519-the-emperor-of-nihon-ja">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1868161-stephanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1868161-stephanie?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1868161-stephanie?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121796224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4717604210809751770">John Flanagan always amazes me. He is a very talented author. There are very few series I would read to the very end if they had more than five books. Until now, the only author series I've read that have been longer than five books are Harry Potter and the first twelve books of The Secrets of Droon. My point? For me to read a series for this long and be willing to read more, the author has to be pretty darn good.<br/><br/>The Emperor of Nihon-Ja was great! I absolutely loved the drama between Evalyn and </span>
  <span id="freeText4717604210809751770" style="display:none">John Flanagan always amazes me. He is a very talented author. There are very few series I would read to the very end if they had more than five books. Until now, the only author series I've read that have been longer than five books are Harry Potter and the first twelve books of The Secrets of Droon. My point? For me to read a series for this long and be willing to read more, the author has to be pretty darn good.<br /><br />The Emperor of Nihon-Ja was great! I absolutely loved the drama between Evalyn and Alyss! It was really awesome when they had to work together without anyone else's supervision. This book focused a little bit on everyone, which I liked and didn't like at the same time. I miss the story having more of an emphasis on Will like in the fifth or sixth books. At the same time though, I liked how the story had a more even focus on everyone. Will is so blind when it comes to girls; it makes me laugh. But that's part of his character. <br /><br />As you can imagine, there's a big battle at the end of the book. One of the best parts about the battle is that fact that Will leads it. He's the commander. Yes, he has help and stuff but he's the kind of like the master mind behind it. In previous battles, we've seen how Rangers usually stand back and pull the strings during a battle. Instead of Halt doing this, Will did. He was like the leader of the group at that point, protecting the Emperor. He's like a mini Halt. I love it!<br /><br />The writing was, as usual, spectacular. Flanagan can really write a battle scene! He's done a great job staying true to the characters all this time. The banter between them all is as enjoyable as ever and is always one of my favorite elements of the book. I really do hope this isn't the last book in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4717604210809751770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/366118005?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer366118005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer154082391720050683">Here we have another entry in the Ranger's Apprentice series. This is an excellent YA series (some volumes are better than others) and I'd recommend it. Some say this is more a series for boys than for girls but I disagree. Even if it started that way it has grown to include the "love stories" of both Will and his best friend and this book was pretty much split in half. The stories of Will and his male friends is half the story while the tale of Alice and the Princess' adventures is the other ha</span>
  <span id="freeText154082391720050683" style="display:none">Here we have another entry in the Ranger's Apprentice series. This is an excellent YA series (some volumes are better than others) and I'd recommend it. Some say this is more a series for boys than for girls but I disagree. Even if it started that way it has grown to include the "love stories" of both Will and his best friend and this book was pretty much split in half. The stories of Will and his male friends is half the story while the tale of Alice and the Princess' adventures is the other half, the viewpoints alternating.<br /><br />If you've followed this series you know that it's been based in a world much like medieval Europe with countries and peoples that roughly correspond with "Earthly" counterparts. Here we meet the people of a land that is roughly (very, very roughly) like feudal Japan.<br /><br />This is a good fast moving adventure story. Don't go to it for detailed history or geopolitics. Do go to it for good characters, good plotting, great action and story telling.<br /><br />It's a YA book but I think it'll stand up well for the parents of those YAs and even for older folks who aren't parents but like a good fantasy story. I can recommend this one, enjoy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="154082391720050683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1546424168" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1546424168" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=older-kids-adults">older-kids-adults</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=asian-themes">asian-themes</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1546424168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16608402668704239092">Another heartwarming and engrossing action-adventure for older kids and adults, featuring Horace, Will, Halt, Alyss, Evanlyn/Princess Cassandra, Gundar Heartstriker the Skandian (see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1524173.The_Sorcerer_in_the_North__Ranger_s_Apprentice___5_' title='The Sorcerer in the North (Ranger's Apprentice, #5) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sorcerer in the North</a>) and Selethen the Irridian Arab (see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2836109.Erak_s_Ransom__Ranger_s_Apprentice___7_' title='Erak's Ransom (Ranger's Apprentice, #7) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Erak's Ransom</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21456821.Scorpion_Mountain__Brotherband_Chronicles___5_' title='Scorpion Mountain (Brotherband Chronicles, #5) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Scorpion Mountain</a>).<br/><br/>As the title suggests, this story is set in ancient Japan (which is also know as Nihon / Nihon-koku, as well as Nippon / Nippon-koku). Horace and friends help the honorable Emperor Shigeru defeat a cowardly usurper. T</span>
  <span id="freeText16608402668704239092" style="display:none">Another heartwarming and engrossing action-adventure for older kids and adults, featuring Horace, Will, Halt, Alyss, Evanlyn/Princess Cassandra, Gundar Heartstriker the Skandian (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1524173.The_Sorcerer_in_the_North__Ranger_s_Apprentice___5_" title="The Sorcerer in the North (Ranger's Apprentice, #5) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sorcerer in the North</a>) and Selethen the Irridian Arab (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2836109.Erak_s_Ransom__Ranger_s_Apprentice___7_" title="Erak's Ransom (Ranger's Apprentice, #7) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">Erak's Ransom</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21456821.Scorpion_Mountain__Brotherband_Chronicles___5_" title="Scorpion Mountain (Brotherband Chronicles, #5) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">Scorpion Mountain</a>).<br /><br />As the title suggests, this story is set in ancient Japan (which is also know as Nihon / Nihon-koku, as well as Nippon / Nippon-koku). Horace and friends help the honorable Emperor Shigeru defeat a cowardly usurper. The focus on fighting as a group in formation (creating a shield wall) and other Roman (Toscanan) battle gear and tactics reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29394.Cursor_s_Fury__Codex_Alera___3_" title="Cursor's Fury (Codex Alera, #3) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Cursor's Fury</a>. There is also a fairly strong focus on the Senshi class and their katana sword.<br /><br />I enjoyed the new character, Mikeru.<br /><br />I felt the cat-fights between Alyss and Evanlyn were overdone, but at least they finally resolved their differences.<br /><br />I enjoyed the humor and the focus on Japanese culture, despite the obvious stereotypes. I also appreciated the intermix of Japanese language.<br /><br />Butterfly. Haha.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16608402668704239092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2965100465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2965100465" />
    <a title="Smaug the Unmerciful Editor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/95618407-smaug-the-unmerciful-editor"><img alt="Smaug the Unmerciful Editor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567608261p2/95618407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2965100465?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Smaug the Unmerciful Editor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Smaug the Unmerciful Editor" href="/user/show/95618407-smaug-the-unmerciful-editor">Smaug the Unmerciful Editor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/11707971-the-emperor-of-nihon-ja">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95618407-smaug-the-unmerciful-editor?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95618407-smaug-the-unmerciful-editor?shelf=unbelievably-dumb">unbelievably-dumb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95618407-smaug-the-unmerciful-editor?shelf=totally-clean">totally-clean</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2965100465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6909723913369276460">I can hear you: <i>Smaug, since you read the other nine books and you hated them all, why the HECK are you reading the tenth one?!</i> Well, it's because I am a wishy-washy old grouch, that's why. I got this far, I might as well finish the series. <br/><br/>Man, where to start? Yet another extremely mediocre book with bad world-building, bad characters, and poorly done plot. Blatant spoilers ahead, by the way.<br/><br/>The whole Japanese thing does not work for John. He basically took the entire Japanese language, culture</span>
  <span id="freeText6909723913369276460" style="display:none">I can hear you: <i>Smaug, since you read the other nine books and you hated them all, why the HECK are you reading the tenth one?!</i> Well, it's because I am a wishy-washy old grouch, that's why. I got this far, I might as well finish the series. <br /><br />Man, where to start? Yet another extremely mediocre book with bad world-building, bad characters, and poorly done plot. Blatant spoilers ahead, by the way.<br /><br />The whole Japanese thing does not work for John. He basically took the entire Japanese language, culture, climate etc. and tweaked things here and there to suit his tastes. Like how all Nihon-Jan are short and dark-haired, sit in a position uncomfortable to Westerners (in real Japanese culture they fold their legs underneath them--- you know, the tea ceremony position. In this book, they sit on their heels, legs apart, like a bunch of barbarians), drink green tea all the time, and have delusions of honor. And what John did for the language --- get this --- he took plain ol' Japanese and just made a few glaring grammatical and alphabetical inconsistencies. He altered the meaning of Will's nickname (Chocho, which means "a little" in Japanese and spelled "chiyo chiyo", means "butterfly" in Nihon-Jan) and for some reason against all grammar made the Nihon-Jan pronounce Horace's name as "Or'ss." I mean, WHAT?! Any dummy who knows even a little bit of the Hiragana alphabet can spell "Horace" in Japanese! I've studied hiragana, one of the Japanese alphabets, so I know quite a bit of pronunciation and such. And Horace could be said like this: Horasu. Not all that hard. I just don't understand how the Nihon-Jan language works. Also, may I add, "Nihon" means "Japan" in Japanese? How's that for originality!<br />More proof for bad language making: the Senshi class ("senshi" means "warrior" in Japanese) is the warrior class (just like feudal Japan), they call the Araluens "gaijin" (which literally means "foreigner"), and they call Halt "Halto" which has the letter L in it. The Japanese cannot pronounce the letter L. But apparently they make an exception for Halt but not for Will, whom they call "Wirru?" I get the feeling that John tried to combine all Asian languages to make the Nihon-Jan language, which would've worked fine if he hadn't made %99 of the culture Japanese. In fact, despite Nihon-Ja being extremely isolated for so long, most of the citizens can speak ENGLISH?! And that Alyss can speak Nihon-Jan?! Like, what the heck! If you stay away from each other for centuries, you can't speak each other's EXTREMELY DIFFERENT languages: rule of thumb.<br /><br />The story was pretty lacking. It was almost exactly the same as ALL OTHER Ranger's Apprentice books with a castle/fortress and/or army. Will teaches the army some amazing, new, incredible effective way to fight (see Battle for Skandia) in which they become almost completely unbeatable. Halt hatches this sort of master plan. Horace either stands around scratching his head telling everyone how dumb he is, beats up people or displays his surprising cleverness in battle tactics. Literally the only reason they added Alyss an Evanlyn (whose name the Nihon-Jan misspell in a stupid way -- E-van-in or something like that when it should be Evu-anrin) was for them to acquire an extra army of apes for the rest of them --- again, an army that comes out of nowhere and is invincible. Also some romance where Evanlyn and Horace decide to get married (why would Evanlyn want to marry such a blockhead? Who knows?) but John could've done that in ANY OTHER BOOK. Also, a note on Horace's weapons: he lost his broadsword so he got a new, invincibly-forged one later. And then he slays a bunch of enemies with it. You know who would win if you pitted a katana-wielding samurai vs. a broadsword-wielding knight against each other? The samurai, of course! His blade is razor sharp and made for speedy slashes. Also, it's thin, so it can get into the cracks between the armor, AND they samurai SPECIFICALLY valued speed over force, so when Horace wins without a scratch, I just can't help but cringe. Nothing is right about the duels.<br />One more thing: the Nihon-Jan apparently don't battle all vs. all: each warrior finds another warrior to duel and then duels him until one of them dies. This is inconsistent with Japanese battling. In the 17th century, they fought like mad. It was total chaos, not honorable, organized duels.<br />The allied Nihon-Jan generals are noble, honorable, willing to give their lives for their even nobler cause, compassionate, and always cool under pressure, while the enemy Nihon-Jan as a whole are dim-witted, blindly obedient, or in the generals' cases, cowardly, greedy, cruel and out-of-control. Not a single enemy leader has any good qualities whatsoever. This is obviously unrealistic, because even HITLER had some good qualities, for crying out loud! He was a great leader of men, charismatic, and he even had a little girl over for strawberry cake because they shared the same birthday! D'awww! (That's not to say he wasn't the devil incarnate: he just wasn't bad ALL the time.)<br />The child, Mikeru, showed an astonishing amount or wisdom and knowing about weaponry, along with all the other farmers. Excuse me, I didn't get the impression that farmers, of all people, made it a point to study who weapons worked and what they should avoid when creating them. They had better things to do, after all, like providing food for their families.<br /><br />As you've probably seen, this book annoyed me to near-death. I'm this far into the series, though, so I'm going to plow on --- mainly because it's a clean fantasy.<br /><br />But if you skip this book, that's fine. Nothing happens that won't be explained in the next books.<br /><br />And the worst part is, I was looking forwards to this one the most, since it was Japanese and stuff.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6909723913369276460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2219447032" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2219447032" />
    <a title="Nigel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61463964-nigel"><img alt="Nigel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513313791p2/61463964.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2219447032?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nigel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nigel" href="/user/show/61463964-nigel">Nigel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=teenage">teenage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2219447032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15456501879806908258">Another entry in the enjoyable Ranger's Apprentice series, a mediaeval fantasy series written for teenagers. I originally borrowed the first of these for my 9yo, but read it myself after realising they were a little too old for him, and have continued to pick them up when I see them at our library. This adventure is set in 'Nihon-Ja' (an easily recognisable feudal Japan), and is derivative of both James Clavell's 'Shogun' as well as the Tom Cruise movie 'The Last Samurai', with samurai warlords </span>
  <span id="freeText15456501879806908258" style="display:none">Another entry in the enjoyable Ranger's Apprentice series, a mediaeval fantasy series written for teenagers. I originally borrowed the first of these for my 9yo, but read it myself after realising they were a little too old for him, and have continued to pick them up when I see them at our library. This adventure is set in 'Nihon-Ja' (an easily recognisable feudal Japan), and is derivative of both James Clavell's 'Shogun' as well as the Tom Cruise movie 'The Last Samurai', with samurai warlords feuding and battling for power, with the help of 'Western' outsiders, in this case our band of adventurers from Araluen. Like many fantasy novels, the actual fantasy world is actually just our world with different place names. So far, this series has featured stints in the Sahara (bedouins, sandstorms etc highly reminiscent of the classic Beau Geste adventure novels), as well as Vikings, Scottish highlanders, and French knights (battling English/Araluen knights). This isn't really a criticism, just an observation, but this lack of originality is, in my limited experience of this genre (YA/teenage), is the main drawback. Overall a fun adventure, recommend for teenagers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15456501879806908258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_299285474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/299285474" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/299285474?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399255007" href="/book/show/8404519-the-emperor-of-nihon-ja">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer299285474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10626686699604466843">Not one of my favorites in the series, which is disappointing since it's the last one (not counting the book of short stories). It's not bad, per se, but it just didn't have that same spark that has made me love this series, in general.<br/><br/>Anyway - Horace has gone to Nihon-Ja (essentially a version of Japan) on a diplomatic sort of thing and, while there, gets embroiled in a political upheaval. Evanlyn, worried about him, joins with Halt, Will and Alyss - and others - to go find him.<br/><br/>A quick not abou</span>
  <span id="freeText10626686699604466843" style="display:none">Not one of my favorites in the series, which is disappointing since it's the last one (not counting the book of short stories). It's not bad, per se, but it just didn't have that same spark that has made me love this series, in general.<br /><br />Anyway - Horace has gone to Nihon-Ja (essentially a version of Japan) on a diplomatic sort of thing and, while there, gets embroiled in a political upheaval. Evanlyn, worried about him, joins with Halt, Will and Alyss - and others - to go find him.<br /><br />A quick not about the "and others". In the beginning of the story Halt, Will and Alyss are helping Toscano and Arrida broker a piece treaty - Selethen being the ambassador from Arrida. Since Selethen is there when Evanlyn shows up to start the quest, he decides to join in.<br /><br />Also, Evanlyn arrives there on a ship helmed by Gundar, one of the Skandians from a previous story.<br /><br />I couldn't help but feel that a lot of this was just maneuvering in order to get as many familiar faces from past stories together as possible for this final story.<br /><br />Anyway, a fair part of the beginning of the story is travelling, and a good portion of the rest of the story is about military engagements. And while it was interesting enough for what it was, it didn't really have the same intensity as a lot of the other fights presented through-out the series.<br /><br />And I guess I was a little miffed that Horace seems to take center stage in this story. Not that I don't like Horace or anything, but since it was the last book in the Ranger's Apprentice series I thought Will should've been in a more pivotal role. <br /><br />Also, the characterizations seemed to be off from time to time. Also, it bugged me that Will was sort of shown as being clueless when it came to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the budding relationship between Horace and Evanlyn, and also between the tension - or reason for the tension - between Alyss and Evanlyn. The former especially bugged me because just in the last story Will mentions Horace's desire to want to spend more time with the princess, and says "good for you" when Horace basically admits his feelings. But in this book we're meant to believe that Will's clueless. It really annoyed me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In some ways I felt like the characterization of Will was off. He felt younger again, more like the Will of his second or third year - not the Will who has graduated and become a Ranger in his own right. But since the events of the book take place after all the others, chronologically, it felt off. So not only does Will not take center stage, but he felt off.<br /><br />Everyone felt a little off, really.<br /><br />I don't know. I would almost have been happier if the story took place earlier in the timeline, because everyone felt younger, if that makes sense. But it very clearly doesn't.<br /><br />Who knows - maybe I'm just disappointed because the series is over, and I never would've been happy with "the last". But I think it's more than that and, overall, while it wasn't a bad story, overall, it was a let down for being the last in the series.<br /><br />(Oh - Tug and Abelard aren't even in this one! Talk about being off... )<br /><br />I think I would've been happier if Book 9 had been the end, to be honest. When I inevitably reread the series, I might even stop with Book 9. Or read Book 10 before Books 8 &amp; 9. <br /><br />Ah well. It wasn't like it was bad enough to sour my feelings towards the series (and that has happened) - but it's a bummer to go out on a down note.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10626686699604466843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1412911603" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1412911603" />
    <a title="rachel ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel"><img alt="rachel ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591333266p2/17290119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1412911603?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rachel ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rachel ☾" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel">rachel ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=young-adult-lit">young-adult-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1412911603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8692737764645730190"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I cannot say that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7592279.The_Emperor_of_Nihon_Ja__Ranger_s_Apprentice___10_' title='The Emperor of Nihon-Ja (Ranger's Apprentice, #10) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Emperor of Nihon-Ja</a> was my favourite <i>Ranger's Apprentice</i> book, because it wasn't. While it wasn't as jarringly disconnected like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1524173.The_Sorcerer_in_the_North__Ranger_s_Apprentice___5_' title='The Sorcerer in the North (Ranger's Apprentice, #5) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sorcerer in the North</a>, it was a little slow and the characters were a little more distant (is that the word I'm looking for?) than usual. <br/><br/>Nihon-Ja was an interesting setting. I love that it was somewhere new, so we got to learn about a new culture and meet new characters that bought something a little different to the story. The Emper</span>
  <span id="freeText8692737764645730190" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />I cannot say that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7592279.The_Emperor_of_Nihon_Ja__Ranger_s_Apprentice___10_" title="The Emperor of Nihon-Ja (Ranger's Apprentice, #10) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor of Nihon-Ja</a> was my favourite <i>Ranger's Apprentice</i> book, because it wasn't. While it wasn't as jarringly disconnected like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1524173.The_Sorcerer_in_the_North__Ranger_s_Apprentice___5_" title="The Sorcerer in the North (Ranger's Apprentice, #5) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sorcerer in the North</a>, it was a little slow and the characters were a little more distant (is that the word I'm looking for?) than usual. <br /><br />Nihon-Ja was an interesting setting. I love that it was somewhere new, so we got to learn about a new culture and meet new characters that bought something a little different to the story. The Emperor was the most adorable character, and it will be sad to see him go! But it was also fantastic that some of our old favourite characters - Evanlyn, Alyss, Gundar, Nils &amp; Selethen - were back. I had missed seeing Evanlyn particularly as she was such a big part of earlier books, but I thought her and Horace's romance was a little forced. He just seemed to blush whenever someone said Evanlyn's name around him... now they are together? <br /><br />The main characters, Halt, Horace &amp; Will, like I said before, were lacking their usual spark. It wasn't hard to notice the lack of their usual banter. Halt seemed rather subdued, and him &amp; Will barely did anything throughout the novel. It was nice to see Horace sticking up for himself at the beginning of the novel, but once Halt got there he sort of stopped and gave the reins to Halt which was disappointing. I didn't like that he thought he was so dependent on Halt.<br /><br />I think the most disappointing thing about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7592279.The_Emperor_of_Nihon_Ja__Ranger_s_Apprentice___10_" title="The Emperor of Nihon-Ja (Ranger's Apprentice, #10) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor of Nihon-Ja</a> was the female characters. This is a very male-dominated story, so when the two female characters we get - Alyss and Evanlyn - came into the story as the jealous, whiny, pathetic, bitchy stereotype I was sorely disappointed. Alyss was plain rude to Evanlyn, and instead of being understanding and diplomatic like she should of been, Evanlyn riled Alyss up. Luckily, during their kayaking trip, the girls did bond and overcome most of their pettiness, which was nice to witness. <br /><br />Overall, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7592279.The_Emperor_of_Nihon_Ja__Ranger_s_Apprentice___10_" title="The Emperor of Nihon-Ja (Ranger's Apprentice, #10) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor of Nihon-Ja</a> wasn't my favourite sequel. It should have been split into two books, and could have easily done so. The story would have flowed better. The battle would have had an ending rather than the pathetic thing we got. Horace and Evanlyn's romance would have had time to bloom. There could have been more time spent on Evanlyn and Alyss' trip, and the groups' trip to Nihon-Ja. But however much I am complaining, I really did love this book. The last 100 pages were back the usual standard, and I only wished the story could have been spread out more so I wouldn't have gotten so sluggish in the middle.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8692737764645730190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1532845556" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1532845556" />
    <a title="Samuel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52174409-samuel"><img alt="Samuel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1532845556?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samuel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samuel" href="/user/show/52174409-samuel">Samuel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1532845556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14713161757001461905">John Flanagan has truly outdone himself once again. This book, by far, is his greatest masterpiece, and one of the best books I have ever read. A collection of action, battle, strategy, friendship, cunning, and romance, this book rejuvenates the vigor and excitement of war, completely enticing the reader. This book is best suited for mature audiences, who will not be frightened by the epitomy of war, but rather accept it and live through the imaginary experience, enlightening themselves in the r</span>
  <span id="freeText14713161757001461905" style="display:none">John Flanagan has truly outdone himself once again. This book, by far, is his greatest masterpiece, and one of the best books I have ever read. A collection of action, battle, strategy, friendship, cunning, and romance, this book rejuvenates the vigor and excitement of war, completely enticing the reader. This book is best suited for mature audiences, who will not be frightened by the epitomy of war, but rather accept it and live through the imaginary experience, enlightening themselves in the rare feeling of war and bloodshed. In the main battles of the book, John Flanagan uses many realistic components that could really exist, such as archers, shields, traps, etc. All main characters in the book are neither ignored nor emphasised, creating a perfect balance so focus does not sway, thus avoiding a loss of attention or boredom. <br /><br />Our heroes Will and Horace are placed in the middle of an perilous uprising, the previously-peaceful country of Nihon-Ja caught in a battle of dramatic proportions, as the noble Emperor is hunted down by his traitorous generals, who want to become king. Engaging the readers in enticing warfare, and the will and want to find out what happens and how it ends. Pure gold, this book is the very definition of perfect in the form of literature and tales. Horace, the knight, and Will, the Ranger, are depicted extremely well and cooperate in such an realistic way that the readers can fully delve themselves into the storyline, and can replace the characters in each of the ‘scenes’ in their imagination. Truly a impeccable book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14713161757001461905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6000690601597998030">A bit long, especially compared to the previous books in the series, but it's totally forgivable because this is the last novel in the series that focuses on Will, and honestly the author's done a long story before. He just broke it up into <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14713719.Rangers_Apprentice__Book_Five_The_Sorcerer_of_the_North__Vol_1_of_2_' title='Rangers Apprentice, Book Five The Sorcerer of the North (Vol 1 of 2) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rangers Apprentice, Book Five: The Sorcerer of the North</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1814843.The_Siege_of_Macindaw__Ranger_s_Apprentice___6_' title='The Siege of Macindaw (Ranger's Apprentice, #6) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Siege of Macindaw</a>. And I would prefer the whole story just be told in one book.<br/><br/>This has the characteristic strengths of Flanagan's writing: strong characters (both male and female), realistic hu</span>
  <span id="freeText6000690601597998030" style="display:none">A bit long, especially compared to the previous books in the series, but it's totally forgivable because this is the last novel in the series that focuses on Will, and honestly the author's done a long story before. He just broke it up into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14713719.Rangers_Apprentice__Book_Five_The_Sorcerer_of_the_North__Vol_1_of_2_" title="Rangers Apprentice, Book Five The Sorcerer of the North (Vol 1 of 2) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">Rangers Apprentice, Book Five: The Sorcerer of the North</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1814843.The_Siege_of_Macindaw__Ranger_s_Apprentice___6_" title="The Siege of Macindaw (Ranger's Apprentice, #6) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Siege of Macindaw</a>. And I would prefer the whole story just be told in one book.<br /><br />This has the characteristic strengths of Flanagan's writing: strong characters (both male and female), realistic human relationships, and a "fantasy" world that is a very thinly reskinned Earth. Flanagan bases his cultures so closely on real historical equivalents that I actually feel it's a good thing because it educates readers about those historical cultures, even if only a little. There are good moments of light humor, a fun running gag about "a term of great respect", and an engaging plot that gives everyone a chance to shine. Well, except that the two rangers Will and Halt don't spend much time exercising their cool "hide, sneak, and surprise" skills. I guess you can't have everything ;).</span>

  <span id="freeText14479737326389638902" style="display:none">I am afraid to say that I was, in fact disappointed. After the first few chapters I new the basic outline for the plot, which to say the least pretty much follows the plot line from the previous books. And by the time I finished I wasn't even happy it say that I figured it out before the ending. I was looking forward to this book in the hope that it would end with a happier note than what I felt when reading the two previous books before. Making Halt a run away prince with a twin brother reminded me of so many stories that I was almost horrified that John Flanagan hadn't thought of something a little more un-original. He is the man the created the Rangers.<br /><br />And be warned for an abrupt ending. It was something that I think everyone was waiting for and happened so suddenly and quickly. And then the book was finished. I just could have thought of a few different directions this book could have gone. Maybe I'm just getting too old to read kids books.<br /><br />Something to read to your sister/brother/kids before bed time? I would suggest this one. Enough action to keep them entertained and the plots so simple they won't get confused.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1465564644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18099130805289895858">Again, this felt like a placeholder book. *sad face* It didn't help that the Alyss/Evanlyn fighting went on for too long; one to three focused arguments would have been fine, but this one had at least four.<br/><br/>Recommended 12+ for violence, scary situations, and maybe mild language? (It's not that much if it's there)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Apun7tew+iC7LA+yvSstmrGrrvbNzox4hzq/boYJwcs4vc48bO4zSBwHu9NK3idFZ/RJPgNDAh/cRPnfS0ozUQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

It wasn't until he wrote a highly uncomplimentary poem about a senior executive at the agency where he worked, however, that his talent was revealed. It turned out one of the company directors agreed with John's assessment of the executive, and happily agreed to train John in copywriting. <br /><br />After writing advertising copy for the next two decades, John teamed with an old friend to develop a television sitcom, Hey Dad!, which went on to air for eight years. <br /><br />John began writing Ranger's Apprentice for his son, Michael, ten years ago, and is still hard at work on the series. <br /><br />He currently lives in a suburb of Manly, Australia, with his wife. In addition to their son, they have two grown daughters and four grandsons.</span>
